deprecate_posargs(deprecation_warning, remappable_names, /):\n101:     \"\"\"\n102:     Function/method decorator to deprecate some or all positional arguments.\n103: \n104:     The decorated function will map any positional arguments after the ``*`` to\n105:     the corresponding keyword arguments and issue a deprecation warning.\n106: \n107:     The decorator takes two arguments: a RemovedInDjangoXXWarning warning\n108:     category and a list of parameter names that have been changed from\n109:     positional-or-keyword to keyword-only, in their original positional order.\n110: \n111:     Works on both functions and methods. To apply to a class constructor,\n112:     decorate its __init__() method. To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n113:     use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n114: \n115:     Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n116: \n117:         def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n118:             ...\n119: \n120:     to::\n121: \n122:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n123:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n124:             ...\n125: \n126:     After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n127: \n128:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n129:             ...\n130: \n131:     Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n132:     parameters or change the remaining ones. For example, this attempt to add a\n133:     new param would break code using the deprecated posargs::\n134: \n135:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n136:         def some_func(request, wrong_new_param=None, *, option1, option2=True):\n137:             # Broken: existing code may pass a value intended as option1 in the\n138:             # wrong_new_param position.\n139:             ...\n140: \n141:     However, it's acceptable to add new *keyword-only* parameters and to\n142:     re-order the existing ones, so long as the list passed to\n143:     @deprecate_posargs is kept in the original posargs order. Create cache key for this IP\n        cache_key = f'rate_limit:{ip}'\n\n        # Get current count from cache\n        count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)\n\n        # Check if limit exceeded\n        if count >= limit:\n            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()\n\n        # First request should be allowed\n        response = self.middleware.process_request(request)\n        self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n    def test_request_exceeding_limit(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that requests exceeding limit return 429.\"\"\"\n        request = self.rf.get('/')\n        request.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        # Set up limit for one IP\n        request1 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request1.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '192.168.1.1'\n\n        request2 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request2.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '192.168.1.2'\n\n        # Set first IP to limit\n        cache.set('rate_limit:192.168.1.1', 100, 3600)\n\n        # First IP should be blocked\n        response1 = middleware.process_request(request1)\n        self.assertIsInstance(response1, HttpResponseTooManyRequests)\n\n        # Second IP should be allowed\n        response2 = middleware.process_request(request2)\n        self.assertIsNone(response2)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=5, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=60)\n    def test_custom_settings_override(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that custom RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS and RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW work.\"\"\"\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n        request = self.rf.get('/')\n        request.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        # Set cache to custom limit\n        cache.set('rate_limit:127.0.0.1', 5, 60)\n\n        # Should be blocked with custom settings\n        response = middleware.process_request(request)\n        self.assertIsInstance(response, HttpResponseTooManyRequests)\n        self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n\n    def test_counter_increment(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that request counter increments properly.\"\"\"\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n        request = self.rf.get('/')\n        request.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        # First request\n        response = middleware.process_request(request)\n        self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n        # Check counter was incremented\n        count = cache.get('rate_limit:127.0.0.1')\n        self.assertEqual(count, 1)\n\n    def test_x_forwarded_for_header(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that X-Forwarded-For header is used for IP detection.\"\"\"\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n        request = self.rf.get('/')\n        request.META['HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR'] = '203.0.113.1, 198.51.100.2'\n        request.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        # RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Maximum number of requests per window (default: 100)\n    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check if the request IP has exceeded the rate limit.\n\n        Returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests (429) if limit exceeded, None otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Get configuration from settings\n        limit = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS', 100)\n        window = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW', 3600)\n\n        # Get client IP address\n        ip = self.get_client_ip(request)\n\n        # Create cache key for this IP\n        cache_key = f'rate_limit:{ip}'\n\n        # Get current count from cache\n        count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)\n\n        # Check if limit exceeded\n        if count >= limit:\n            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()\n\n        # Increment counter and set cache with expiration\n        cache.set(cache_key, count + 1, window)\n\n        return None\n\n    def get_client_ip(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the client IP address from the request.\n\n        Checks X-Forwarded-For header first (for proxied requests),\n        then falls back to REMOTE_ADDR.\n        \"\"\"\n        forwarded_for = request.META.get('HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR')\n        if forwarded_for:\n            # X-Forwarded-For can contain multiple IPs; take the first one\n            return forwarded_for.split(',')[0].strip()\n        return request.META.get('REMOTE_ADDR', '')\n","numLines":64,"startLine":1,"totalLines":64}}}

RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Maximum number of requests per window (default: 100)\n    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check if the request IP has exceeded the rate limit.\n\n        Returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests (429) if limit exceeded, None otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Get configuration from settings\n        limit = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS', 100)\n        window = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW', 3600)\n\n        # Get client IP address\n        ip = self.get_client_ip(request)\n\n        # Create cache key for this IP\n        cache_key = f'rate_limit:{ip}'\n\n        # Get current count from cache\n        count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)\n\n        # Check if limit exceeded\n        if count >= limit:\n            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()\n\n        # Increment counter and set cache with expiration\n        cache.set(cache_key, count + 1, window)\n\n        return None\n\n    def get_client_ip(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the client IP address from the request.\n\n        Checks X-Forwarded-For header first (for proxied requests),\n        then falls back to REMOTE_ADDR.\n        \"\"\"\n        forwarded_for = request.META.get('HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR')\n        if forwarded_for:\n            # X-Forwarded-For can contain multiple IPs; take the first one\n            return forwarded_for.split(',')[0].strip()\n        return request.META.get('REMOTE_ADDR', '')\n","numLines":64,"startLine":1,"totalLines":64}}}
